9/29/19, 8:58 PM - Shikhar Vaish: class Node: 
    def __init__(self, key): 
        self.data = key 
        self.left = None
        self.right = None

def buildTree(level, ino): 

    if ino : 
        for i in range(0, len(level)): 
            if level[i] in ino: 
                node = Node(level[i]) 
                io_index = ino.index(level[i]) 
                break
        if not ino: 
            return node 
        node.left = buildTree(level, ino[0:io_index]) 
        node.right = buildTree(level, ino[io_index + 1:len(ino)]) 
        return node 

def minDepth(root): 
    if root is None: 
        return 0 
    if root.left is None and root.right is None: 
        return 1
    if root.left is None: 
        return minDepth(root.right)+1
    if root.right is None: 
        return minDepth(root.left) +1 
      
    return min(minDepth(root.left), minDepth(root.right))+1

def calc(input1,input2,input3):
    return minDepth(buildTree(input2, input1) ) 

print (calc([4,2,5,1,6,3,7],[1,2,3,4,5,6,7],7))

10/11/19, 4:53 AM - Shabd Saran: and you've also defined as Iterator as a generic type, i can't really put a type in it because initially its of type <String, List<String>> but later you're using it as <Integer, List<String>>.

10/11/19, 5:02 AM - Shabd Saran: package com.mujdell2019.hackathon.utils;

import java.util.ArrayList;
import java.util.HashMap;
import java.util.Iterator;
import java.util.List;
import java.util.Map;
import java.util.Map.Entry;

import org.springframework.context.annotation.Scope;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Component;

@Component
@Scope("singleton")
public class QueryUtil {

	private HashMap<String, HashMap<String, Integer>> attrMap;
    private List<String> attrList;
    private int priceHashStart, priceRangeSize, priceStart, priceEnd;
    private List<String> parseOrder;
    
    
    /*
	    Constructor: QueryMap 
	    @param: HashMap<String, List<String>> valueMap
	            expects a HashMap denoting attribute name as string
	            mapped to a list of possible values of String type
	*/
	public QueryUtil (List<String> attrList, HashMap<String, List<String>> valueMap, int priceStart, int priceRangeSize, int priceEnd) {
	    
	    // calculate maxIntervalSize of hashValue of attribute-value pair
	    int maxInterval = 0;
	    Iterator<Map.Entry<String, List<String>>>valueMapIterator = valueMap.entrySet().iterator();
	    while (valueMapIterator.hasNext()) {
	        Entry<String, List<String>> pair = valueMapIterator.next();
	        maxInterval = pair.getValue().size();
	    }
	    maxInterval += 100;
	
	    // memorize hashValue of each attribute-value pair
	    this.attrMap = new HashMap<String, HashMap<String, Integer>>();
	    for (int intervalStart = 11, attrIndex=0; attrIndex<attrList.size() ; intervalStart += maxInterval, attrIndex++) {
	        String attr = (String) attrList.get(attrIndex);
	        attr = attr.trim().toLowerCase();
	        
	        // price hash is calculated dynamically based on range
	        // price will be received as extra-filters from application during search
	        if (attr.equals("price"))
	            continue;
	
	        List<String> valueList = valueMap.get(attr);
	        HashMap<String, Integer> valueIntegerMap = new HashMap<>();
	        for(int relativeIndex = intervalStart, listIndex = 0; listIndex < valueList.size(); relativeIndex+=7, listIndex++) {
	            String value = valueList.get(listIndex);
	            valueIntegerMap.put(value, relativeIndex);
	            priceHashStart = relativeIndex + 8;
	        }
	
	        this.attrMap.put(attr, valueIntegerMap);
	    }
	
	    this.attrList = attrList;
	
	    this.priceStart = priceStart;
	    this.priceRangeSize = priceRangeSize;
	    this.priceEnd = priceEnd;
	}
	
	/*
	    Method: parseQuery
	    returns a list of predefined integers that represent a query
	    returns an empty list if no mapping was found
	    @param String queryString: the string that was queried by user
	    @param HashMap<String, String> extraFilter: additional filters added by user 
	    @return List<Integer>: list of hash values of attributes
	*/
	public List<Integer> parseQuery(String queryString, HashMap<String, String> extraFilter) {
	    queryString = queryString.trim().toLowerCase();
	    String[] query = queryString.split(" ");
	
	    ArrayList<Integer> hashList = new ArrayList<Integer>();
	
	    for (int attrIndex=0; attrIndex<attrList.size(); attrIndex++) {
	        String attr = attrList.get(attrIndex);
	        HashMap<String, Integer> valueMap = attrMap.get(attr);
	        boolean found = false;
	        
	        if (!attr.equals("price")) {
	            Iterator<Entry<String, Integer>> valueMapIterator = valueMap.entrySet().iterator();
	            while (valueMapIterator.hasNext() && !found) {
	                Map.Entry<String, Integer> valuePair = valueMapIterator.next();
	                String possibleValue = (String) valuePair.getKey();
	                int valueIndex = searchValue(query, 0, query.length, possibleValue);
	                
	                if (valueIndex == -1) continue;
	                
	                hashList.add( getHash(attr, possibleValue) );
	                found = true;
	            }
	        }
	
	        if (!found) {
	            if (extraFilter.containsKey(attr))
	                hashList.add(getHash(attr, extraFilter.get(attr) ));
	            else hashList.add(0);
	        }
	    }
	
	    if (extraFilter.containsKey("price"))
	        hashList.add( getHash("price", extraFilter.get("price")) );
	    else hashList.add(0);
	
	    return hashList;
	}
	
	/*
	    Method: getHash
	    returns a unique predefined integer that is mapped to attribute-value pair.
	    returns 0 if pair was not found.
	    For the attribute, hash is calculated dynamically; does not use pre-defined value
	    @param String attr
	    @param String val
	    @param int: hashvalue
	 */
	 private int getHash(String attr, String val) {
	     if (attr.equals("price")) {
	         int priceVal = Integer.parseInt(val);
	         for (int hash = priceHashStart, price = priceStart; 
	             price + priceRangeSize <= priceEnd ; 
	             price += priceRangeSize, hash++) {
	                 if (price <= priceVal && priceVal <= price+priceRangeSize)
	                     return hash;
	         }
	
	         return 0;
	     }
	
	     if (!attrMap.containsKey(attr)) return 0;  // if attribute was not found
	 
	     HashMap<String, Integer> valueMap = attrMap.get(attr);
	     Iterator<Map.Entry<String, Integer>> valueMapIterator = valueMap.entrySet().iterator();
	     while (valueMapIterator.hasNext()) {
	         Map.Entry<String, Integer> pair = valueMapIterator.next();
	         String possibleValue = (String) pair.getKey();
	         if (possibleValue.indexOf(val) != -1)
	             return (Integer) pair.getValue();
	     }
	     
	     return 0;
	 }
	 
	 /*
	     Method: searchValue
	     returns first index of array found, such that key is a substring of arr[index]
	     returns -1 if no matches were found
	     @param String[] arr : query array
	     @param int start    : index from where the search starts(inclusive)
	     @param int end      : index where the search ends(exclusive)
	     @param String key   : search element
	     @return index: search result
	 */
	 private int searchValue(String[] arr, int start, int end, String key) {
	     for (int i = start; i < end; i++)
	         if (key.indexOf(arr[i]) != -1) return i;
	     return -1;
	 }
}

SALE

10/13/19, 5:53 PM - Shikhar Vaish: shabd

	problem statement
		we were given a problem to develop a product recommendation system that can help Dell increase its revenues and also increase engagement of dell customers.

	how are we solving it
		we have come up with a solution that consists of two unique features, game-specific search engine and Automated sale concept.

		now, let me explain you the first one. so, here's how its done. you go to the homepage of our website, switch to the game tab, and now you can see a list of popular games.
		let's say you are a really big FIFA fan and you want to buy a new gaming laptop, but you don't really know the game specifications of FIFA. what you will do here is simply click on FIFA 20. When you do that, we will get the specifications of this game and search our database for matching laptops. And now you have it, all the laptops you can buy to play your favorite game.

		Now, my friend Shikhar will explain you our next feature

shikhar
	
		Another aspect of our solution is to help the dell administrators view product analytics 
		on the dell store. This is offered through a Admin Portal:

		The Portal will allow us to view product details such as Most Viewed product and Least Bought Product.

		moreover, the adminstrator can view the order conversion rate for a specific product for the last 12 months.

		We're also introducing the concept of Automated Sale. So, what it does is it selects the 3 products that have least bought count in the current month and calculates a discount rate using their order conversion rate.

		Now, the adminstrator will have complete control over this sale, ie, he can add/remove the items that are up for sale, change the discount rate and even cancel the sale.

		Now, my friend Shivang will explain the rest of the features on our website.

shivang
		General Recommendation
		Search products
		User behaviour Tracking
		Tech stack, Architecture

Sakshi
		ML

11/6/19, 11:18 AM - Shabd Saran: Dear Students (of Digital Image Processing only)

 

Following is the syllabus for MTE-2 in your course CS 1553 Digital Image Processing

 

Frequency Domain Enhancement: Introduction to Image Transforms, Fourier Transform, 2D DFT calculations.
Restoration: Various Spatial Filtering methods, Noise Models, various type of Noises, Restoration Using Inverse Filtering.
Image Coding and Compression Lossless Compression, Lossy Compression, Compression Ratio, Entropy, Huffman Coding, Arithmetic Coding, Run Length Coding, JPEG.


As you know this course is also supported by MOOC course learning Mode from the course Image and Video Processing: From Mars to Hollywood with a Stop at the Hospital. https://www.coursera.org/learn/image-processing

Topic from WEEK -1 to WEEK-4 can be helpful for reading the above contents form the mentioned MOOC Course.
As MST-2 and Final Exam are going to be OPEN BOOK mode. It is advised to student to support the learning of MOOC by self-study from TEXT / REFRENCE Books and Practice more numerical problems.
Two Books and One Hand Written Notes are allowed.


Following Books are suggested:

RC Gonzalez and RE Woods, ‚ÄúDigital Image Processing‚Äù
S Jayaraman et al , ‚ÄúDigital Image Processing‚Äù
Sridhar, ‚ÄúDigital Image Processing‚Äù
Alasdair McAndrew, ‚ÄúDigital Image Processing using MATLAB‚Äù (E - Book PDF Attached)

https://arxiv.org/abs/1607.02533
Adversarial examples are designed to fool a classifier. We can take an image that is classified correctly using any neural network, then backprop through the model to find which changes we need to make in order for it to be classified as something else. These changes can be quite small, such that a human would hardly notice a difference
